Well Evaluation
Marathon Oil Company
Dellana Ward USA 14-7H
Figure 1. H&P rig 386 drilling the Marathon Oil Company,
Dellana Ward USA 14-7H well in Dunn County, North Dakota in October of 2014.
INTRODUCTION
The Marathon Oil Company, Dellana Ward USA 14-7H [Lot 1 Section 18 , T146N, R92W; 783'
FNL & 1,016' FWL] is located approximately 8.5 miles north and 7 miles east of the town of
Dunn Center in Dunn County, North Dakota (Figure 1). The Dellana Ward USA 14-7H will be
a dual section well, with an approximately 10,000' long lateral designed to further oil production
in the area. The surface will be drilled using freshwater drilling fluid, while the vertical and
curve sections will use diesel invert drilling fluid. Well plans called for the vertical section to be
drilled to a kick off point of 9,681' measured depth (MD). The curve would then be built at a
rate of 12.00º/100' and would land in the middle of the Middle Bakken target interval set by the
Marathon Oil Company geologist. After casing the vertical and curve, the lateral will be drilled
using a salt-water drilling fluid. Geo-steering and directional drilling techniques will be used to
maintain maximum exposure to the target zone. The planned lateral section was to be drilled
north at an azimuth of 358.21º. Upon anticipated completion of the Dellana Ward USA 14-7H,
the hole will be prepared for casing and production evaluation. The hole will be lined and will
use a 30 stage artificial fracture technique to maximize the production value.
OFFSET WELLS
Three offset wells were used as primary controls while drilling the Dellana Ward USA 14-7H.
Data including gamma-ray signatures and electric logs from nearby offset wells were used to
determine a prognosis of formation tops. These wells include:
The Roehr USA 34-7H [SE NW Sec. 18, T146N, R92W] which is located
approximately 1,300' SE of the Dellana Ward USA 14-7H (Figure 2). This well
was drilled by Marathon Oil Company. It is a lateral Bakken well and is currently
active.
The FLB-Askew 1-14A [SE SE Sec. 14, T146N, R93W] which is located
approximately 9,000' SW of the Dellana Ward USA 14-7H. This well was drilled
by ANR Production Company and is currently dry.
The Rohde USA 14-20H [SW SW Sec. 20, T146N, R92W] which is located
approximately 10,000' SE of the Dellana Ward USA 14-7H. This well was drilled
by Marathon Oil Company. It is a lateral Bakken well and is currently active.
The vicinity of these wells to the subject well's surface location made them ideal for generating a
well-rounded prognosis of formation tops. Other offset wells, including the Halliday 2-12-1H-1
were also used for structure control during the curve landing and lateral.
ENGINEERING
The well was spud on September 28, 2014 by H&P's rig 386. The surface hole was drilled using
a 13 ½" rock bit and 5" drill pipe to a depth of 2,080' MD. A freshwater based drilling fluid
was used during this operation. The surface hole was then isolated and cemented, using 9 " 36
# J-55 casing set to 2,065' MD. On September 30th, 2014, freshwater was displaced by invert
diesel drilling fluid, with mud weights fluctuating between 9.65-10.25 pounds per gallon.
Utilizing one 8 ¾" PDC Security bit, the vertical hole was drilled to a kick-off point (KOP) of
9,680' MD in 48.3 drilling hours. The curve build began on October 5th, 2014. Two bottom-
hole assemblies (BHA) were used to build the curve. Curve assemblies used were two 8 ¾" PDC
Security bits, two 2.38° fixed NOV motors, and one MWD tool that recorded surveys and
gamma-ray data throughout the curve. The curve was drilled to a total depth of 10,895' MD in
24.6 drilling hours. After completing the curve, 7" casing was set and cemented to 10,878'MD
using 32# P-110 and L-80. In preparation for drilling the lateral portion of the well, invert diesel
drilling fluid was displaced with salt water drilling fluid. Mud weights ranged from 8.2-10.15
pounds per gallon. One 6" PDC Smith bit and one Security bit were used along with a 1.40° and
a 1.50° fixed mud motor. An MWD tool was used in conjunction with each BHA. These two
assemblies drilled to total depth in 70.2 drilling hours.
The Dellana Ward USA 14-7H reached a total depth of 20,969' MD on October 16, 2014, at a
closure direction of 358.18° and a true vertical depth (TVD) of 10,339.94'. The bottom-hole
location is: 11,174.31' north and 355.43' west of surface location or approximately 212.48' FNL
& 660.57' FWL, Lot 4 Section 6, T146N, R92W (Figure 2).

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods
Geologic analysis was provided by two Sunburst Consulting well-site geologists. Gas levels
were monitored using a digital gas detector and chromatograph. The chromatograph was
interfaced with a Pason electronic data recorder. The Pason relayed data such as measured depth,
bit depth, and pump stroke information to the MController gas monitoring software.
MController returned gas in the form of total gas units (100 units = 1% methane equivalent in air) to
be logged and displayed across the drilling location. Multiple component gases (methane, ethane,
propane, and butane) and their concentrations were recorded in parts per million. ¼" Poly-Flo ®
tubing was used to direct gas into the chromatograph where the data was then translated and
lagged to the correct depth. Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the
supervision of well-site geologists. Analysis and evaluation of gas and drill cuttings began in the
Kibbey Formation at 8,050' MD and ended in the Middle Bakken at 20,969'. Cuttings were
observed in wet (isopropyl alcohol) and dry conditions under a binocular microscope.
Lithology
Note: There were no electric logs run for the Dellana Ward USA 14-7H because of its proximity
to the Roehr USA 34-7H well. All depths while drilling the vertical and curve are referenced to
driller's depth.
The Kibbey Formation (Big Snowy Group) consists of red-orange siltstone with some gray to
red interbedded silty sandstone. There is a very distinct layer of limestone, referred to as the
"Kibbey Lime", was logged at 8,081' TVD (-5,838' MSL) and consists of light to medium gray
mudstone. There is a thin layer of anhydrite right above the limestone that marks the top of the
"Kibbey Lime" marker.
The Charles Formation (Madison Group) consists of limestone and a large amount of
evaporates including salt and anhydrite. The Charles First Salt was logged at 8,234' TVD
(-5,991' MSL). The Base Last Salt was logged at 8,685' (-6,442' MSL).
The Mission Canyon Formation (Madison Group) consists of light to dark gray-brown
limestone and was logged at 8,867' TVD (-6,624' MSL). Some areas contain algae laminations,
fossil fragments, and trace amounts of intercrystalline porosity with dead oil staining.
The Lodgepole Formation (Madison Group) (Figure 3) is characterized by medium to dark
gray argillaceous limestone. The top was logged at 9,463' TVD (-7,220' MSL) and is marked by
a transition from limestone to argillaceous limestone. The "False Bakken" is a layer of shale
near the bottom of the Lodgepole Formation. It was logged at 10,289' TVD (-8,046' MSL). The
"Scallion" is a layer of limestone at the base of the formation and was logged at 10,302' TVD
(-8,059' MSL).
The Bakken Formation (Devonian-Mississippian) is comprised of two layers of black,
petroliferous shale and a mixed clastic and carbonate middle and lowermost member. The
lowermost member of the Bakken Formation is recognized as the Proghorn which was not seen
while drilling the Dellana Ward USA 14-7H. The Upper Bakken Shale Member (Figure 4) was
logged at 10,314' TVD (-8,071' MSL). This member is recognized by its high gamma counts, an
increase in rate of penetration (ROP), and elevated total gas units. The Middle Bakken Member
(Figure 5) consists of three distinct lithologies and was logged at 10,332' TVD (-8,089' MSL).
A layer of siltstone lies directly below the upper member. Below the siltstone lies a laterally
discontinuous layer of fossiliferous (packstone) limestone. Below the limestone is a gray to
brown silty sandstone.
Figure 3, 4, & 5. Wet cuttings of Lodgepole Formation (left), upper Bakken shale (middle) and middle
Bakken packstone/silty sandstone (right).
Geo-steering
The prognosis called for a landing target of 10,357' TVD, at an inclination of 90°. The
prognosis for the top of the target was 10,352' TVD and the bottom of the target was 10,362'
TVD, allowing for a 10' target window. The landing target was set 20' below the base of the
Upper Bakken Shale, and 5' below the top of the target window. Using gamma-ray data, well-
site geologists were able to correlate formation tops from the Dellana Ward USA 14-7H to
nearby offset wells in the area to assure an accurate landing. Several changes to the landing
target were made as tops varied significantly in the uphole markers. Before completion of the
tangent by the directional drillers, a landing target of 10,347' TVD was determined. Upon
observation of lower level tops, the target was again altered to 10,352' TVD. The wellbore
landed 1' low to the initial target at 10,353' TVD. This placed the wellbore 6' below the top of
our original target window. The target window was altered before commenced drilling of the
lateral-due to a thicker layer of packstone in the Middle Bakken than expected. The revised
target window encompassed depths between 10,352' TVD and 10,362' TVD. This revision
placed the wellbore 1' below the top of the target window.
Target zone, gamma ray signatures were very consistent at 75-90 (API) gamma. The only
variation in this was an increase at the extreme top of the target window to a larger wavelength
gamma of 65-100 (API). The other variation was 1-2' above the bottom of the target window,
where a decrease to 50 (API) was observed.
The Middle Bakken target window was entered at approximately 10,878' MD (10,352' TVD).
The well-bore was maintained in the target zone for 74% of the lateral. The formation rose 12.0'
TVD over the course of the lateral, with a gross apparent dip of +0.04° (Figure 6).

Gas and Oil Show
The label used to quantify gas for this well was units (100 units is equal to 1% methane
equivalent in air). The first time any significant gas was logged was a gas show of 27 units in the
Charles Formation, at a depth of 8,459' MD. Gas shows continued sporadically throughout the
remainder of the vertical portion of the well and varied in size from 10-51 units. Background gas
averaged 10 units in the vertical portion of the well until an increase to an average of 25 units
was observed at the start of the Lodgepole Formation. Gas shows increased after the False
Bakken marker was reached. The largest gas show observed during the curve was a slide gas of
1,319 units at a depth of 10,810' MD within the Middle Bakken Member.
Throughout parts of the lateral, light green to medium brown oil was observed coming over the
shakers and in sample. Background gas varied from 400-4,500 units. Average background gas
for the lateral was 3,500 units. Gas shows were common with the largest not related to
connection gases, being 5,499 units at 14,232' MD (Figure 7). The largest connection gas
followed shortly thereafter with 6,168 units at 14,328' MD. Gas was circulated through the
buster for the entire length of the lateral, and starting at 11,200' MD a flare was observed until
total depth was reached. The flare reached as high as 25' with 10' being the most common size.
Due to the high amount of gas recorded, casing back-pressure was held starting at 18,650' MD
and continued until total depth was reached.

SUMMARY
The Marathon Oil Company, Dellana Ward USA 14-7H is a Middle Bakken lateral well. Spud
commenced on September 28, 2014 and the well was drilled to a kick off point of 9,680' MD.
The curve was landed at 10,353' TVD, 1' below the revised target top. Samples from the target
interval presented as light gray silty sandstone, containing very fine intergranular porosity and
light spotty brown oil staining. Throughout parts of the lateral, light green to medium brown oil
was observed coming over the shakers and in sample. Background gas in the lateral ranged from
400-4,500 units, with gas shows as high as 6,168 units. Gas was circulated through the buster for
the entire duration of the lateral and casing pressure was held, starting at 18,650' MD. Flares as
large as 25' were observed. The well-bore was maintained within the target interval for 74% of
the lateral section. The Dellana Ward USA 14-7H reached a total depth of 20,969' MD on
October 16, 2014 after 19 drilling days.
Respectfully Submitted,
Brandon Jasper
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.

Lithology
Dellana Ward USA 14-7H
Lagged samples were caught by rig crews under the supervision of Sunburst geologists in 30' intervals from 8,050'
to 20,969' (TD). The drilling fluid was diesel invert in the vertical and curve sections and post-casing operations
was replaced with a brine solution for the lateral. All samples were caught within compliance of North Dakota state
regulations as well as the policies and procedures of Marathon Oil Company. Samples were examined wet and dry
using a binocular microscope. Dried cuttings were then boxed and sent to the state of North Dakota as well as the
Marathon Oil Company sample storage facility.
Drilling in the Kibbey Formation
Kibbey "Lime"
8,084' MD/ 8,081' TVD (-5,838')
8050-8080 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray to medium gray, occasional tan, microcrystalline, friable to firm,
earthy texture, no visible porosity; common SILTSTONE: light red to brown, rare dark brown, trace cream to tan,
friable to firm, sandy in part, sub-blocky, earthy texture, calcite cemented, no visible porosity
8080-8110 SILTSTONE: light red to brown, rare dark brown, trace cream to tan, friable to firm, sub-blocky, earthy
texture, calcite cemented, no visible porosity; occasional LIMESTONE: as above
8110-8140 ANHYDRITE: off white to milky, gray, soft, massive, amorphous texture; occasional SILTSTONE: as
above
8140-8170 SILTSTONE: light red to brown, rare dark brown, trace cream to tan, friable to firm, sub-blocky, earthy
texture, calcite cemented, no visible porosity; occasional ANHYDRITE: off white to milky, gray, soft, massive,
amorphous texture
8170-8200 SILTSTONE: light red to brown, rare dark brown, trace cream to tan, friable to firm, sub-blocky, earthy
texture, calcite cemented, no visible porosity; occasional ANHYDRITE: off white to milky, gray, soft, massive,
amorphous texture
8200-8230 SILTSTONE: light red to brown, rare dark brown, trace cream to tan, friable to firm, sub-blocky, earthy
texture, calcite cemented, no visible porosity; occasional ANHYDRITE: off white to milky, gray, soft, massive,
amorphous texture

HORIZONTAL WELL
DELLANA WARD USA 14-7H
LOT1 Section 18-146N-92W
Dunn County
Well File # 29030
Dear Natalie:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 23505, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than
the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within
the 1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sec 6&7T146N R92W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for
filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must
remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted. Due to drainage adjacent to the well site, a dike is required surrounding the entire location.
Tool error is not required pursuant to order. MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field
Inspector Ashleigh Devenberg at 701-290-3277 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing
point is: 983'N. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well
head is: 11186'N, 516'W.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Natalie Menge
August 1, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division,
Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number,
drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m.
and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours
or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey
contractor shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion.
Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director
may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is
hereby granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing
on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well
records wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall
permit the Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or
controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to
have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time
upon request. The information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and
shall be available only to the Commission and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE: Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 250 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

Flowback Strategy
Anticipated First Production date
Anticipated first production date for the three wells site is January 2015. It is expected that it wil be connected to a
gas sales pipeline at first production.
Multi-well startup
It is currently planned for two wells to be flowed back together and the third to flowback after this. The flowback
period is expected to last approximately 3-10 days for each wel .
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates
Average Gas rate from the wel pad during flowback is anticipated to be around 1,600 MSCFD.
Average Oil rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 2,400 bopd

requirements.
